### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic corpus formulas stand where this theme's thesis is that an entrypoint is a contract plus plumbing, both variants promise the same thing, classify by mode, specify with REQ-RUST contracts, design L1/L2/L3 before coding, verify by risk, return the seven-part contract, and differ only in how they wire the agent to depth
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's authors separated what the agent must promise from where the agent must read, so the promise ported cleanly across platforms while the plumbing had to be rebuilt per habitat, a separation that made the port cheap and the deltas legible
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: entrypoints that mix promise and plumbing cannot port this way, every relocation edit risks touching doctrine, and the Claude variant's dead absolute paths show the failure in miniature, plumbing decayed while the promise around it stayed true
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the thesis governs entrypoint design, the promised doctrine's own content is the deep references' subject

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the two variants demonstrate asymmetric decay, the shared contract has no environment dependencies and cannot rot locally, while both plumbing layers rot on their own schedules, absolute paths at machine change and relative links at folder moves, so entrypoint maintenance is almost entirely plumbing maintenance

- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the variants target different agent platforms with different context economics, the Codex file assumes progressive loading with the entrypoint read first and depth pulled on demand, the Claude file assumes an installed skill with a resident reference, so variant choice follows the consuming platform's loading model
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: cross-platform consumption misfires concretely, a progressive loader following the Claude variant has no Context Strategy to sequence its reads, and an install-based agent following the Codex variant may pull four references it could have had resident

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario

- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the theme's artifacts are consumed at deployment and maintenance time rather than during Rust work itself, so its journeys are meta-journeys, about the skill files, while the Rust-work journeys belong to the deep references the entrypoints route into

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside what both entrypoints instruct about performance, reject vague claims like faster without thresholds, include performance in the verification mix when risk warrants, and report measurable evidence in the gate results, threshold discipline enforced at the specification stage before any code exists
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the entrypoints position performance verification as a requirements problem, the REQ-RUST template's measurable-behavior clauses force units at contract-writing time, so performance rigor is front-loaded into specification rather than retrofitted at review
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: work specified with vague speed claims cannot be performance-verified afterward regardless of benchmark quality, the missing thresholds make every measurement unanchored, which is why both variants reject the claims at intake rather than at gate time

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside this theme's real scale limits, the two-variant structure stops scaling gracefully at the third platform port, where pairwise delta tables give way to a needed common-skeleton specification, and the skill's own coverage claim bounds it to application-level Rust, both variants decline unsafe-heavy, lock-free, and proc-macro-heavy defaults explicitly
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because pairwise comparison is quadratic in variants exactly as mirror diffs are in copies, and the guardrails' declined defaults are authored limits that no port can widen, the same two limit classes the transplant theme found, combinatorial growth and inherited coverage edges
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: past the port limit, delta tables multiply and drift independently, and past the coverage limit, consumers get entrypoints that confidently route kernel-grade concurrency questions into references that decline them, coverage failure by confident routing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding the pair structure and the skill's inherited coverage, the deep references' internal scale seams belong to their themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name both limits with triggers, a third variant triggers extraction of the shared skeleton into a platform-neutral specification with per-platform plumbing files, and out-of-coverage requests route to specialist sources the corpus does not currently hold
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the third-variant trigger would retroactively fix the pair's existing ambiguity, extracting the skeleton forces the Miri question to be decided once in the neutral file instead of differing silently per platform, scale pressure as the forcing function that resolves accumulated porting debt, growth as the repair opportunity
